  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d99ed70c-e1e9-484c-81e7-6f8b6f562f2e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText10826397654157962594" style="display:none">King Jorg Ancrath is twenty now—and king of seven nations. His goal—revenge against his father—has not yet been realized, and the demons that haunt him have only grown stronger. Yet no matter how tortured his path, he intends to take the next step in his upward climb.<br /> <br />Jorg would be emperor. It is a position not to be gained by the sword but rather by vote. And never in living memory has anyone secured a majority of the vote, leaving the Broken Empire long without a leader. Jorg plans to change that. He’s uncovered the lost technology of the land, and he won’t hesitate to use it.<br /> <br />But he soon finds an adversary standing in his way, a necromancer unlike any he has ever faced—a figure hated and feared even more than himself: the Dead King.</span>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/23886792-steven-laidlaw"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/23886792-steven-laidlaw">Steven Laidlaw</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    As explained earlier in the series, the builders messed with metaphysical forces and tilted reality off it's axis. This is how supernatural occurrence<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    As explained earlier in the series, the builders messed with metaphysical forces and tilted reality off it's axis. This is how supernatural occurrences are possible (monsters, necromancers, *-sworn, etc).<br /><br />Upon the realisation that his son would never be safe, Jorg died to reunite with William (the Dead King). From the depths of the afterlife, he used his knowledge of how belief shapes the world to shift reality back to where it was meant to be by turning the wheel. The wheel itself was just a manifestation of belief, and could have been anything.<br /><br />This was only possible by the Ancrath brothers, as foretold in Fexler's prophecy. So now, they averted the other two shitty options, and put reality back to the way we know of it today.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>

  <span id="freeText2368716327839994163" style="display:none">Just couple of ratings needed to reach 40,000! <br /><br />All reviews very much appreciated :)<br /><br />---------------<br />Finished the Broken Empire trilogy and want more? <div id="review_623386412" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623386412" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/623386412?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007439065" href="/book/show/15804760-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer623386412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3382444254792026269"><b>”I failed my brother. I hung in the thorns and let him die and the world has been wrong since that night. I failed him, and though I’ve let many brothers die since, that first pain has not diminished. The best part of me still hangs there, on those thorns. Life can tear away what’s vital to a man, hook it from him, one scrap at a time, leaving him empty-handed and beggared by the years. Every man has his thorns, not of him, but in him, deep as bones. The scars of the briar mark me, a calligraphy</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3382444254792026269" style="display:none"><b>”I failed my brother. I hung in the thorns and let him die and the world has been wrong since that night. I failed him, and though I’ve let many brothers die since, that first pain has not diminished. The best part of me still hangs there, on those thorns. Life can tear away what’s vital to a man, hook it from him, one scrap at a time, leaving him empty-handed and beggared by the years. Every man has his thorns, not of him, but in him, deep as bones. The scars of the briar mark me, a calligraphy of violence, a message blood-writ, requiring a lifetime to translate.”</b><br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/TheBrokenEmpire2_zpsc98d076f.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534002049i/26111266.jpg" alt=" photo TheBrokenEmpire2_zpsc98d076f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>The Prince, The King, The Man</b><br><br>Jorg Ancrath is king of seven kingdoms at the tender age of twenty. He did not achieve this feat with political intrigue. Oh no, that would have taken too long and required the type of patience of which he has very little. At fourteen he could swing a sword as well as any grown man. He is a natural born leader of rogues, thieves, and murderers and soon learns how to best use their skills to obtain what he desires. He has seven principalities, but he didn’t come so far so fast to stop there. He wants to rule the entire Broken Empire. <br><br>You are either with him or you are <s>against him</s> dead. <br><br>We don’t know what kind of man Jorg would have become if he had not witnessed the brutal deaths of his brother and mother while he hung in the thorns, hooked, bleeding, and too scared to rip himself loose. His father made it clear that the wrong son died. William was better at everything. Jorg might have spent his days whoring, gambling, and drinking, taking full advantage of being the neerdowell son, but with William dead and his father rejecting him... well... he went psychotic. <br><br><i>”Whatever lay broken inside me had started to wind too tight to be ignored. I would shake the world until its teeth rattled if that was required to have it spit out an answer. Why?</i><br><br>The trilogy is set in the future. The Builders who despite the wonderful technologies or maybe because of them destroyed themselves. It was the <b>day of a thousand suns</b> taking the world from the height of civilization back to medieval in about the time it took everyone to say…<b>oh shit</b>. <br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/d15d0974-f68f-4f6b-8965-7ab6f0368a83_zps8de80a9f.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534002049i/26111264.jpg" alt=" photo d15d0974-f68f-4f6b-8965-7ab6f0368a83_zps8de80a9f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Anybody who has studied a bit of history knows that in medieval times if there were laws they were only enforceable by those with the brawny strength to uphold them. Might made right and with Jorg’s warped; and yet, at times astute view of world he is a man of his time. <br><br><i>”Dark times call for dark choices. Choose me.”</i><br><br>Jorg will sacrifice any friend no matter how precious or how loyal to achieve his ends. He will rape, pillage, and murder because he is bored or annoyed or needs something to chase away the pain in his head. Now here is where Mark Lawrence works his own bit of necromancy. Despite the fact that Jorg is this despicable little bastard with a moral compass that spins with the wind you will start to like him. It will scare you. It might even make you retch. You will spend time with heart palpitating and all that you hold dear being re-evaluated when you realize that Jorg has reached into your soul and touched a darkness that you didn’t even know was there. <br><br>You will not be able to return to Mayberry. <br><br>Jorg has a wife, an arranged marriage, that by some twist of the universe has paired two people that are entirely suited to each other. There are no illusions, no love, no trust, but something more important is formed a bond of mutual respect. Miana is pregnant and it makes me tremble to think of this child, forged in such fury, let loose upon a world trying to climb one step closer to civilization. He will either be the savior or the final destruction. One of the enemies that Jorg has made is the pope of Rome, a bloated, fat woman that confirms the reason why gluttony should be a sin in a world where so many go hungry. She sends an assassin.<br><br><i>”Sometimes it cuts to see other men more passionate than I about the things that I should care for. I knew that if the Pope’s assassin had killed Miana and our unborn child I would have grieved. But also I knew that some terrible part of me, down at the core, would have raised its face to the world with a red grin, welcoming the chance, the excuse, for the coming moments of purity in which my revenge would sail upon a tide of blood. And I knew that rage would have swept away everything else, including sorrow.”</i><br><br>Jorg responds by deciding to rebuild a church which when one first hears of this you might think that Jorg is growing up thinking more about repairing alliances than thinking about revenge. You would be wrong. The pope has to come and consecrate a new church which would put her within sword length and as we know that has proven to be a too close to continue breathing for enemies of Jorg in the past. <br><br>The Congression is being called and all the leadership from all the principalities is coming together for a vote for King of the Broken Empire. The Dead King is marching his armies with the intent to rule what is left of humanity. His army builds as they kill people and turn them into their puppet soldiers. Jorg by murder, mayhem, and trickery is trying to obtain the votes necessary to be declared King of the known world as The Dead King’s army knocks at the gates. <br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/BrassBalls_zpsd62842c8.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534002049i/26111265.jpg" alt=" photo BrassBalls_zpsd62842c8.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Brass Balls award goes to…Mark Lawrence.</b><br><br>I don’t normally read fantasy. This is the first fantasy series that I’ve read all the books. A tip of the hat to Mark Lawrence to have the brass balls to end a successful series at three volumes. Part of the reason that I don’t read fantasy is generally by the time I take notice of a series it already has ten volumes or more. The characters have been facsimiled so many times they are merely a gray shade of themselves in the text. Lawrence is getting out clean with Jorg showing all the sharp edges of a man ready to step out of the text into the real world, and believe me you better have your sword drawn when you see the tip of his nose emerging. <br><br>These books are bloody, brutal, dark, and marvelous. I do not contest any reviewers decision to give this book series one star or three stars or five stars. It is a series that will force the reader to evaluate their own capacity for violence. We all like to think of ourselves as good people, and we can maintain that illusion usually right up until the time we are truly tested. <br><br><br>Prince of Thorns (The Broken Empire, #1) review. You'll have to forgive the brevity as I was a pup reviewer then. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195689927" rel="nofollow noopener">Link for my Prince of Thorns review</a><br><br>King of Thorns (The Broken Empire, #2) review. A much more Keetenesque review. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/401394978" rel="nofollow noopener">Link for my King of Thorns Review</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3382444254792026269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1763808816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763808816" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1763808816?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425256541" href="/book/show/18342280-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763808816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15450025837323627314"><b>3.5/5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Emperor of Thorns marks the conclusion of The Broken Empire trilogy and I must say, despite my lukewarm and dislike towards the first and second book, I end up enjoying the last book in the trilogy more than I expected.<br/><br/>Jorg, now 20 years old, is on his way to become the Emperor of the Broken Empire but there’s a looming threat that’s coming for him and the Broken Empire itself, the Dead King. EoT managed to wrap the main storyline wonderfully, the entire climax of the trilogy between </span>
  <span id="freeText15450025837323627314" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 Stars</b><br><br>Emperor of Thorns marks the conclusion of The Broken Empire trilogy and I must say, despite my lukewarm and dislike towards the first and second book, I end up enjoying the last book in the trilogy more than I expected.<br><br>Jorg, now 20 years old, is on his way to become the Emperor of the Broken Empire but there’s a looming threat that’s coming for him and the Broken Empire itself, the Dead King. EoT managed to wrap the main storyline wonderfully, the entire climax of the trilogy between Jorg and the Dead King plus the ending is gripping and well written. It’s safe to say Jorg’s story that we followed since he was 10 years old ended satisfyingly. However, I feel like the end section deserve more screen time since it ended in a bit of a rush and at the same time, there are still some things unexplained specifically on the history sections and how exactly the Dead King came to be.<br><br><b>Picture: Chibi Emperor Jorg by peastri</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493527749i/22626397._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story is again told in the same method as before, divided between three main sections, Jorg’s 20 years old present day, 5 years earlier which continues straight after King of Thorns past section but before KoT present section <i>(weird isn’t it?)</i> and another female perspective, Chella the necromancer. Honestly, I prefer Chella’s Story more than Katherine’s diary back in KoT which were almost completely pointless imo. Chella’s story does provide information and depths to the main story and it’s told in 3rd person POV which added color to the narrative.<br><br>There’s also one more reason why the plot in EoT is the best out of the trilogy. It’s the fact that there is only one or two <b>‘Dream sequence’</b> here. Let me tell you this, I despise the entire dream sequence of the trilogy, 90% of the time when it appeared, it ended up hurting the pacing and I can’t wait for it to be over as soon as possible. Every dream sequence is hard to digest and most of the time are pointless to the main storyline, it’s there to show Jorg’s obsession and relationship with his aunt, Katherine, which at the end, doesn’t have any closure whatsoever and made me wonder, what was the point of reading all that.<br><br>Despite this trilogy having a huge problem in the scarcity of compelling side characters, Jorg is one of the most unique protagonist in fantasy I ever read. He’s pretty much the sole main driving factor of the trilogy and it’s really awesome to see his growth from the first book up to the end of EoT. He’s a really complex character, don’t get me wrong, he’s an asshole, a scum, ruthless, selfish and violent but he has his protective and redeeming factors. This book gives the conclusion on his journey into his redemption, whether he succeeded or not, I’ll leave it for you to find out. <br><br><b>Picture: A scene from the book <i>(Interior Artwork from Broken Empire Omnibus edition by Jason Chan)</i></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457003314i/18305877._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For the world-building section, the overdue explanation, while still unsatisfactory is finally here. Some <b>“Gary-Stu”</b> moments from King of Thorns finally received a proper explanation, especially regarding where Jorg received the Builder’s Tools. I do wish there is more information on the history and everything about the Builder, there is so much potential to make this series better but hey, in the end this trilogy has always been about Jorg.<br><br>I must state once again that Mark’s prose is a thing of beauty and authenticity, it’s original, philosophical and sadly, a double edged blade for me. I don’t think it was a good idea for me to binge read this trilogy. I love binge read, it’s what I always do but on this case, I think this time the prose damaged my rating. There are a lot of parts that could be trimmed down, especially on Jorg’s inner monologue that go on and on more than necessary that made the trilogy tedious to read. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“No half measures. Some things can’t be cut in half. You can’t half-love someone. You can’t half-betray, or half-lie.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>Overall, I think The Broken Empire trilogy may be one of most overrated trilogy of all time for me.</b> I struggled heavily to finish it that I don’t think it’s a good idea to read it right after reading Red Sister. To compare them is probably unfair since they’re written differently but it’s really obvious from the comparison in quality that this is Mark’s debut trilogy once you read it. I can’t say the same for Red Queen’s War (haven’t read it yet) but none of the book in this trilogy ever came close to the quality of Red Sister.<br><br>I’ll recommend this trilogy to anyone who’s looking for a complete anti-hero and unique grimdark read but if you’re looking for a fantastic grimdark fantasy series, my recommendation is to look for a different series such as The First Law trilogy by Joe Abercrombie.<br><br><b>Series review:</b><br><br>Prince of Thorns: <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763808112?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">3/5 Stars</a>
</u><br><br>King of Thorns: <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763808348?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">2.5/5 Stars</a>
</u><br><br>Emperor of Thorns: <b>
  <u>3.5/5 Stars</u>
</b><br><br>The Broken Empire Trilogy: <b>
  <u>9/15 Stars</u>
</b><br><br><b>Picture: The Broken Empire <i>(Omnibus edition cover)</i></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493527819i/22626400._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>You can find this and the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Booknest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15450025837323627314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_573406113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/573406113" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1259463-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469679884p2/1259463.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/573406113?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/1259463-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007439065" href="/book/show/15804760-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer573406113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10692831984204212719">You may be wondering why/how I am reviewing a book that is not due to be published for several months. The answer is I couldn't wait, in more ways than one.<br/><br/>I've written about Mark Lawrence before. <a href='http://www.petervbrett.com/2011/09/09/on-blurbing-and-thorn-princes/' rel='nofollow noopener'>I reviewed the first book in this series, Prince of Thorns, on my blog a couple years ago</a>. I enjoyed it so much I happily offered quotes to Mark's publishers to be used on the second volume, King of Thorns, even before I'd had a chance to read it. I secured an advance copy of KoT, but again was too bus</span>
  <span id="freeText10692831984204212719" style="display:none">You may be wondering why/how I am reviewing a book that is not due to be published for several months. The answer is I couldn't wait, in more ways than one.<br /><br />I've written about Mark Lawrence before. <a href="http://www.petervbrett.com/2011/09/09/on-blurbing-and-thorn-princes/" rel="nofollow noopener">I reviewed the first book in this series, Prince of Thorns, on my blog a couple years ago</a>. I enjoyed it so much I happily offered quotes to Mark's publishers to be used on the second volume, King of Thorns, even before I'd had a chance to read it. I secured an advance copy of KoT, but again was too busy to get to it until after the publication date.<br /><br />You can see <a href="http://www.petervbrett.com/2013/01/04/king-of-thorns-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">my King of Thorns review here</a>, but the tl:dr version is I loved it. Loved it so much that despite the fact I often counsel eager readers that anticipation for a book can be a special pleasure in and of itself, I set about pulling strings to get a copy of Emperor. I knew the book was written, though advance reads and Netgalleys were still some time away.<br /><br />This is one of the places where being a published author living in NY can pay off. I know pretty much the whole staff at Ace/Roc, the imprint of Penguin that publishes Mark. Many of us drink together, and they often ask me to blurb new authors. But this time, my sources were no avail. The book was still in raw manuscript, without even a copyedit, and they were reluctant to release it in that form. I then tried Voyager, the UK publisher Mark and I both share. Again a fail.<br /><br />So I went right to the source. I have met Mark twice, been to his home, and shared many a correspondence with him. Through a combination of cajoling, false promises of friendship, and a little emotional blackmail, I wore him down enough to secure a word document, swearing to keep it secret and safe, deleting as I read so there would be no chance it might get out before its time. Indeed, the manuscript has already been returned to the digital ether, so don't ask.<br /><br />I'm not one for spoilery reviews, especially so far before publication, but that need not stop me from telling you to drop whatever else you're reading and start the Broken Empire trilogy. If you've already read the first two, the third is worth pre-ordering, or marking your calendar to buy in-store on release day. First week sales can make or break an author's career, and Mark deserves to see his star rise.<br /><br />In Emperor, we return to the character of Jorg, an amoral, violent, selfish protagonist, who nevertheless is posessed of an impressive charm and the soul of a poet. Told in the first person, Jorg's recounting of horrid events, conflicting emotions, and even the everyday pains and pleasures of life is told in a vivid prose filled with brutal honesty, profound reflection and brilliant metaphor. Every sentence is carefully crafted, a work of art and a pleasure to read.<br /><br />As with King of Thorns, the story weaves through different times in Jorg's life. One might say "past" and "present", though those are in some ways meaningless terms when speaking of the life of a fictional character set in a fictional world. In the "present", Jorg continues his path toward the Empire Throne, the last hope of uniting the broken remnants of humanity to single purpose once more. Though of course, Jorg does not want the throne for such lofty reasons. In truth, he does not know what he would do with it should he win. He just hates being told he cannot have something. On his way, he struggles with the kernels of real family for the first time since his childhood, fearing that caring too deeply will make him weak, and vulnerable to his enemies.<br /><br />The "past" of the story is no less compelling, providing background and context for the struggles in the "present" as Lawrence strips away the garments covering his world and letting us at last have a good long look at the underlying philosophy, magic and technology that makes it tick.<br /><br />Lawrence fills the last book of his series with unexpected twists and turns, and an ending I don't think readers are at all likely to predict. I certainly didn't.<br /><br />Broken Empire was an amazing series, and I eagerly anticipate Lawrence's next literary effort, whatever it may be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10692831984204212719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_466462138" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/466462138" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/466462138?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007439065" href="/book/show/15804760-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer466462138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14785087582874809212">Mark Lawrence likes to claim that <a href='http://mark---lawrence.blogspot.com/2013/04/i-am-not-my-character-duh.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>authors are not their characters</a>, but I think we need to look at the facts.<br/><br/><b>Jorg Ancrath:</b><br/><br/>1. Single-mindedly takes the world by storm.<br/>2. Spreads his wit (among other things, blood and guts included).<br/>3. Flips everything on its head, traditions, magic, you name it.<br/>4. Encourages blasphemy and the slaughter of innocents.<br/>5. Will stop at nothing to reach his goals of claiming the title of Emperor.<br/><br/><b>Mark Lawrence:</b><br/><br/>1. Single-mindedly takes the fantasy world by storm.<br/>2. Sprea</span>
  <span id="freeText14785087582874809212" style="display:none">Mark Lawrence likes to claim that <a href="http://mark---lawrence.blogspot.com/2013/04/i-am-not-my-character-duh.html" rel="nofollow noopener">authors are not their characters</a>, but I think we need to look at the facts.<br /><br /><b>Jorg Ancrath:</b><br /><br />1. Single-mindedly takes the world by storm.<br />2. Spreads his wit (among other things, blood and guts included).<br />3. Flips everything on its head, traditions, magic, you name it.<br />4. Encourages blasphemy and the slaughter of innocents.<br />5. Will stop at nothing to reach his goals of claiming the title of Emperor.<br /><br /><b>Mark Lawrence:</b><br /><br />1. Single-mindedly takes the fantasy world by storm.<br />2. Spreads HIS wit (and probably other things we won't name here).<br />3. Flips the fantasy world on its head with his antihero fantasy filled with modern technology and countless subverted tropes.<br />4. Encourages blasphemy and the slaughter of innocent bloggers and authors (through words only of course ... hopefully).<br />5. Will stop at nothing to reach his goals of claiming the David Gemmell Legend Award.<br /><br />We're not fooled Mr. Lawrence, no not by a long shot. The next thing we'll see is Mark kicking around Joe Abercrombie's decapitated head.<br /><br />And yes, this is to say, Emperor of Thorns was excellent. The perfect conclusion to an excellent trilogy. It's actually hard to imagine that Lawrence is a debut author and this his debut series. <br /><br />The writing is up there with Joe Abercrombie, filled with great one-liners and quotes at each turn of the page. The following were literally within a page of each other and I could add so many more:<br /><blockquote>"When a decision is inevitable you may as well take it as quick as possible so that you still have something left to deal with whatever consequences may arise." (p. 172 Hardback)</blockquote><br /><blockquote>"When you're in a dark place, and your light is going to run out before too long, you get on with things. It's a wonder to me how few people apply that same logic to their lives." (p. 173)</blockquote><br />It's also just about impossible to stop reading this fascinating character Lawrence has created. Jorg Ancrath is compelling from the first page even when you quickly learn how really terrible he can be. I think there's a lot to going out and doing, accomplishing those things you set out to do whether it's looks feasible or not and Jorg does it all. I honestly do think that there's a lot of Lawrence in Jorg or vice-versa just because of the things that Lawrence himself has overcome. Publishing traditionally is difficult enough, but he can also literally say he is a rocket scientist. He even has a family of four, one of whom is severely disabled (and she is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/345229304" rel="nofollow noopener">publishing amazing stories that my son absolutely loves</a> btw!). This is a man who sets out to accomplish what he puts his mind to and makes it happen too. (Nothin' going on here GR police, nothing at all.)<br /><br />Really the only negative thing I can say is that the timeline gets a little crazy by this last volume. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260303614" rel="nofollow noopener">King of Thorns</a> introduced a portion of the book that took us back "four years earlier" and which portion continues into Emperor of Thorns. The only problem is that it's a year later in the present so "four years" becomes "five years earlier," which later in the book (spoiler alert!) becomes four years earlier even though it is still called "five years earlier." Make sense? There are also flashbacks in the present time that add to the timeline fun, but it's nothing that takes you longer than a moment or two (days? not me, no way) to puzzle out, if that. I'm glad the reader is trusted enough to figure it all out, we can't all be rocket scientists can we? :)<br /><br />Lawrence asks us what happens if the good guy can't make it to save the day and you have to settle for the guy who has done terrible things. The guy you really shouldn't have to root for but who will get the job done. Is it worth it? It's amazing how well he pulled that off. Brutal fantasy that will make you cringe, that will make you think, and that you can't stop reading. Mark Lawrence is in for a terribly long writing career and Emperor of Thorns is about as perfect an ending as you can get. <br /><br />4.5 out of 5 Stars (super duper highly recommended with cherries on top)<br /><br /><b>The Broken Empire Trilogy:</b><br />1) Prince of Thorns (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148700863" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a>)<br />2) King of Thorns (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260303614" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a>)<br />3) Emperor of Thorns</span>
  <a data-text-id="14785087582874809212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1064087129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1064087129" />
    <a title="Petros Triantafyllou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35342421-petros-triantafyllou"><img alt="Petros Triantafyllou" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1064087129?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petros Triantafyllou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petros Triantafyllou" href="/user/show/35342421-petros-triantafyllou">Petros Triantafyllou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064087129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12722845870244037627">Emperor of Thorns is Mark Lawrence's greatest work up to date (The Wheel of Osheim is out). <br/><br/><i>"If i come back from Congression and I'm still not Emperor, I'm not going to be in the mood for excuses."</i><br/><br/>Emperor of Thorns, just like it's predecessors, is featuring two different POVs of the same character. One in the past, covering the time period between the events of the second and third book, while the other, in the present, is following Jorg's tale in the path of conquering and uniting the Broken Em</span>
  <span id="freeText12722845870244037627" style="display:none">Emperor of Thorns is Mark Lawrence's greatest work up to date (The Wheel of Osheim is out). <br /><br /><i>"If i come back from Congression and I'm still not Emperor, I'm not going to be in the mood for excuses."</i><br /><br />Emperor of Thorns, just like it's predecessors, is featuring two different POVs of the same character. One in the past, covering the time period between the events of the second and third book, while the other, in the present, is following Jorg's tale in the path of conquering and uniting the Broken Empire, and crowing himself Emperor. The stakes are now high,and every King is for himself. Or maybe not? If you have already finished the previous two installments, you know exactly what to expect. Exceptional plot arc, controversial and unexpected circumstances, and enough existential dilemmas to leave the book aside and ponder the meaning of life, is what characterizes Mark's work.<br /><br /><i>“Hurt spreads and grows and reaches out to break what’s good. Time heals all wounds, but often it’s only by the application of the grave, and while we live some hurts live with us, burning, making us twist and turn to escape them. And as we twist, we turn into other men.” </i><br /><br />Emperor of Thorns is providing the perfect closure for the critical acclaimed The Broken Empire trilogy, what has now come to be known as one of the greatest fantasy trilogies of our century. <br /><br />You can find more of my reviews over at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://BookNest.eu/">http://BookNest.eu/</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12722845870244037627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1345376197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1345376197" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1345376197?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=grimdark">grimdark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1345376197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10793819912826506788">Originally reviewed at <a href='http://bookwraiths.com/2015/10/07/emperor-of-thorns/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths Reviews</a><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/652573480' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Prince of Thorns</i>
</a> was a seminal work in the fantasy genre. Jorg Ancrath a sociopathic protagonist who became both loved and reviled — seemingly in equal measure. The cry for “<i>More Thorns!</i>” overpowering. Quickly, Mark Lawrence turned <i>Thorn</i>‘s into an epic trilogy; a rousing tale of madness, mayhem, machinations, and meditations on the human condition. And with this final volume, the author has gifted readers with a fitting conclusion, remaining true to </span>
  <span id="freeText10793819912826506788" style="display:none">Originally reviewed at <a href="http://bookwraiths.com/2015/10/07/emperor-of-thorns/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths Reviews</a><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/652573480" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Prince of Thorns</i>
</a> was a seminal work in the fantasy genre. Jorg Ancrath a sociopathic protagonist who became both loved and reviled — seemingly in equal measure. The cry for “<i>More Thorns!</i>” overpowering. Quickly, Mark Lawrence turned <i>Thorn</i>‘s into an epic trilogy; a rousing tale of madness, mayhem, machinations, and meditations on the human condition. And with this final volume, the author has gifted readers with a fitting conclusion, remaining true to Jorg ‘s destructive nature yet giving him a measure of redemption.<br /><br /><i>Emperor of Thorns</i> begins with our favorite Ancrath tantalizingly close to realizing his lifelong ambitions. At twenty years old, Jorg is already king of seven nations, secure in his power, soon to have an heir, and the annual concave to elect an Emperor of the Broken Empire is fast approaching. While he is not certain of being elected to the throne, Jorg has a plan; one that will allow him to assume the reigns of power.<br /><br />What stands in Jorg’s way — as always, it seems — is his abusive father as well as the rising threat of the Dead King, who has completed his conquest of the Drowned Isles and has turned his necrotic eyes upon the continent. And so the tables are set for a final role of the dice for Jorg to either win all or lose all!<br /><br />Interspersed in the tale of Jorg’s procession to the Imperial Conclave is the flashback scenes that Mark Lawrence has made a centerpiece of this series. Here he goes back to Jorg’s time on the Horse Coast years before, detailing his quest to uncover the technology of the ancients in the nuclear wastelands of the peninsula and the further journey that these discoveries produce.<br /><br />Lastly, there are a few chapters scattered throughout focusing on Chella. This female necromancer has hounded Jorg throughout the trilogy, and here the narrative spotlights her . . . more as a way to introduce and detail the Dead King than for any other reason.<br /><br />As I mentioned earlier, this novel was a fitting ending to the trilogy. An action-packed extravaganza that was equal parts sociopathic mayhem and philosophical pronouncements as well as two journeys of discovery by Jorg with tidbits of world building, rousing fights and his grimace worthy actions in equal measures.<br /><br />Is it as awe-inspiring as <i>Prince of Thorns</i>?<br /><br />Not in my estimation. But worth is in the eyes of the beholder, and my preference for book one might be nothing more than just that: my personal preference of one good thing over the other. Because, honestly, I can’t point to anything that did not feel right about this book. It had wonderful pacing. It showed real growth in the characters. It made revelations about Jorg, his world, and the magic permeating it. Its flashbacks chapters even satisfactorily completed the story begun in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/734092353" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>King of Thorns</i>
</a>. It reveals the Dead King in all his dark might and glory. And in the final conclusion it had the perfect emotional mix of realism, cynicism, and hope to cap this epic journey.<br /><br />If I was forced to name anything in the book that I did not find wholly appealing, it probably would be the pacing of the final few chapters before Jorg and the Dead King finally meet. It just seemed very rushed. Mark Lawrence frantically attempting to wrap this epic series up as quickly as possible.<br /><br />All in all, The Broken Empire is a fantasy series that will long be remembered by fans and detractors alike. A series that went somewhere that no other fantasy epics had truly ever been . . . at least, uber popular series. And I for one am very glad that I set aside my disillusion with book two and completed Jorg Ancrath’s journey, because it was quite the ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10793819912826506788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_859373081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/859373081" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/859373081?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer859373081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer354275196058334344">A wonderful, surprising, and worthy ending to the Thorns trilogy. If you’ve followed Jorg Ancrath through the first two books, it shouldn’t shock you that Jorg does not give you the ending you might expect, but it’s an ending that makes perfect sense. As with the past two volumes, this book jumps around in time, from Jorg’s journey to the seat of the empire to vote for a new emperor, back to his earlier journeys through Hispania and Afrique in search of power and answers. Looming on the horizon </span>
  <span id="freeText354275196058334344" style="display:none">A wonderful, surprising, and worthy ending to the Thorns trilogy. If you’ve followed Jorg Ancrath through the first two books, it shouldn’t shock you that Jorg does not give you the ending you might expect, but it’s an ending that makes perfect sense. As with the past two volumes, this book jumps around in time, from Jorg’s journey to the seat of the empire to vote for a new emperor, back to his earlier journeys through Hispania and Afrique in search of power and answers. Looming on the horizon is the Dead King, a mysterious force who has raised armies of the dead and bent powerful necromancers to his will. Eventually, Jorg will have to face both the Dead King and the other players in the internal struggle for the throne of the empire. How he manages this . . . well, let’s say he employs his typical Jorgian style and panache. There will be blood. It was hard to say goodbye to Jorg and his story, but I’m anxious to read Lawrence’s future books set in the Broken Empire. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="354275196058334344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_902546583" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/902546583" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/902546583?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425256541" href="/book/show/18342280-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer902546583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8350022891462759922"><i>"Dark times call for dark choices. Choose me."</i><br/><br/>Jorg of Ancrath, the Prince of Thorns, the boy who would be emperor, is back at long last. Our maliciously fascinating antihero is finally on his way to the holy city of Vyene. Escorted by the legendary Gilden Guard, Jorg is ready to make his way to Congression, the gathering of all the Hundred taking place every four years where they come together in the emperor’s palace to choose who among them shall take up the ever vacant throne of the Broken Emp</span>
  <span id="freeText8350022891462759922" style="display:none"><i>"Dark times call for dark choices. Choose me."</i><br /><br />Jorg of Ancrath, the Prince of Thorns, the boy who would be emperor, is back at long last. Our maliciously fascinating antihero is finally on his way to the holy city of Vyene. Escorted by the legendary Gilden Guard, Jorg is ready to make his way to Congression, the gathering of all the Hundred taking place every four years where they come together in the emperor’s palace to choose who among them shall take up the ever vacant throne of the Broken Empire.<br /><br />But as Jorg finds the achievement of his ultimate ambitions to be closer than ever before, new complications arise in the most distant corners of the Empire. In the sands of Liba on the coast of Afrique, the caliph is intent on murdering Jorg's family. And in the far north, on the Brettan Isles, the mysterious and ghostly character known as the Dead King has conquered everything with his horde of corpses from the Deadlands. All of the Hundred are his enemies, but the only one to truly catch his interest is Jorg Ancrath. In the end, all the threads are woven together at the Congression in Vyene.<br /><br /><i>"We have both walked black paths, lady. Don't think that mine leads back into the light. Of all those that tried to guide me, of my father, of the whispers from the thorn bush, of Corion's evil council, the darkest voice was ever mine."</i><br /><br />Mr. Lawrence's writing continues to be every bit as good as it was in the two previous books of the series. The character of Jorg Ancrath, though, is not as appealing to me as he has been before. Several events occur in this book which make him falter at times, lighting sparks of goodness, fallibility and even uncertainty in this glorious villain. And while noone are really infallible, this does something to Jorg, and takes away some of what made this series so incredibly fascinating in the first place.<br /><br />Just like in <i>King of Thorns</i>, the narrative of this book is divided into three parts. Firstly, of course, there's the tale of the present, of Jorg Ancrath en route to congression to claim the emperor's throne for himself. The second part takes place five years earlier, where Jorg has just uncovered the assassination attempt on his grandfather, and strives to bring vengeance upon those responsible, guided by the ghosts of the Builders themselves. There was in my opinion a bit too much of this part, taking away much of the focus from the main story. I understand that the reader needed to know more about Jorg's past to understand what drives his ambitions, but this part was at times a bit slow and overdone. The last part, though... was absolutely brilliant. The viewpoint of the necromancer Chella - aptly named 'Chella's story' - also takes place in the present, with Chella also on her way to Congression in Vyene as the representative of the dreaded Dead King, whose intentions and identity remain elusive even to her. Here we get a lot of insight into the main antagonists of the story, both Chella herself and her dark master.<br /><br />Then there's the ending. The ending to <i>King of Thorns</i> was definitely the single greatest moment of this trilogy, and sadly I cannot say that the ending to <i>Emperor of Thorns</i> managed to live up to that. For one thing, it felt extremely rushed. The story in the first half of the book moved quite slowly, but in a good way, and at times I was wondering if this was indeed going to be a five-star book. But the book allows no more than around 80 pages for the events at Congression, and everything moved forward way too fast to be good. The scheming and political manipulation was limited to a small number of sentences. Only a handful of the Hundred were even mentioned by name, and the so-called 'hidden hands' behind the thrones were completely absent. I also have to say that mostly everything that happened within the walls of Vyene was quite predictable. But despite my issues, the ending itself was good enough and an absolutely worthy ending for a character like Jorg Ancrath.<br /><br />I liked this book. Out of the three books of the Broken Empire trilogy, I would have to say this is number three in more than one way, but I still liked it. The final verdict from this humble reader is 3.5 stars, but the series as a whole quite certainly deserves four (hence the rating). For those of you who have already read the first and the second book and enjoyed them, you <i>will</i> enjoy this one as well, no matter if you share my opinion or not. For those of you who have not read any of them, it's time to do so. Lawrence's tale from the Broken Empire is something of a fresh breath of air into the fantasy genre, and it certainly deserves to be read. At least it has my recommendation.<br /><br /><i>"All of us have our lives. All of us our moment, or day, or year. And Jorg of Ancrath assuredly had his, and it has been my place to tell it."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8350022891462759922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17327586385259745109"><p>I am completely blown away. What a great ending to a great series!</p><p>Jorg is on his way to Congression knowing he must become Emperor and unite the Hundred against the Dead King. Jorg knows that only united will they be able to stand against him.</p><p>As with the other books in the series, the author bounces between several time periods to tell this story. The process creates a captivating world dominated with strong characters you can't help but enjoy. Jorg more than any other shines. I was never sure i</p></span>
  <span id="freeText17327586385259745109" style="display:none"><p>I am completely blown away. What a great ending to a great series!</p><p>Jorg is on his way to Congression knowing he must become Emperor and unite the Hundred against the Dead King. Jorg knows that only united will they be able to stand against him.</p><p>As with the other books in the series, the author bounces between several time periods to tell this story. The process creates a captivating world dominated with strong characters you can't help but enjoy. Jorg more than any other shines. I was never sure if I loved or hated him. The graphic violence continues in this book and can be quite shocking at times.</p><p>The book is an absolute pleasure to read. The author has created not only a detailed and believable world but the language he uses to describe it is completely immersive. Don't get me wrong there are not pages of description, not at all. Some how the story flows and the plot moves along but this expansive world grows around you as you read and suddenly it's like you're there. Mark Lawrence is easily one of the most skilled writers I have ever read.</p><p>Absolutely great series!</p></span>

<div id="review_882126715" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/882126715" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/882126715?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=1-star-reads">1-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer882126715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16464390110036931653"><b>
  <u>This is a book I really wanted to like. And this is a series I thought I’d love.<u></u></u>
</b><br/><br/>Now I know I’m arguing against the tide, Mark Lawrence is one of the leading names in grimdark fantasy. He has done exceptionally well for himself. I just don’t get on with the way he writes. I hate the way he puts words together and I hate his characters. His stories just don’t work for me. And I’m not going to attempt to objectify my opinion here and talk about literary quality. I am happy to say that it is my </span>
  <span id="freeText16464390110036931653" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>This is a book I really wanted to like. And this is a series I thought I’d love.<u></u></u>
</b><br><br>Now I know I’m arguing against the tide, Mark Lawrence is one of the leading names in grimdark fantasy. He has done exceptionally well for himself. I just don’t get on with the way he writes. I hate the way he puts words together and I hate his characters. His stories just don’t work for me. And I’m not going to attempt to objectify my opinion here and talk about literary quality. I am happy to say that it is my <i>personal</i> experience only. I feel that for the right readers, this series would be fantastic as the reading stats on here alone demonstrate. <br><br><b> So what did I hate?</b><br><br>Jorg. I fucking hate Jorg. I disliked him to the point that I was longing for his death the entire way through (which would never happen because he is the lone protagonist.) In here everything I hated about him persisted to be evident in his overbearing and arrogant personality. He didn’t grow or change just became more like himself if that’s even possible. He was also ridiculously overpowered and a times felt like an invincible video-game character. I could never invest in his character of suspend disbelief to the point where I thought he might die or suffer. <br><br>That being said, his character is what drove me to finish a series I was quite clearly hating. I wanted to see if he had a moral rejuvenation. I wanted to see if he grew as a person and, at least on some level, begin to understand that he is a vile little bastard. I was, of course, disappointed but it kept me reading. His dream sequences were also nonsensical and were just painful to read and added very little to the story. I can honestly say I didn’t like anything about the book and I was glad to finish it and be rid of the revolting protagonist. <br><br>Another issue I had here was how everything was perfectly wrapped together and concluded. For me the series was a bit of a mess (this isn’t a criticism) but there were bits of story all over the place and everything seems to slot into this neat little parcel that’s the climax of this book. And for a series that has felt a little random (by random I mean dictated by the randomness in which life can take you) everything was forced into this ending. It felt odd. It felt uncomfortable. <br><br><b>What of his other books?</b><br><br>I could never like this series, which is largely due to my personal reaction to its protagonist. So I was willing to give the author another go and I did read <i>A Prince of Fools</i> which I really didn’t like (but that was for a whole different set of reasons.) At this point, I can safely say that this author just isn’t for me. I feel like I should try one of his newer books, but after disliking four of his books I think I might know what my opinion will be. It’s safer to try a different author I think. <br><br><u> The Broken Empire Trilogy </u><br>1. <i>Prince of Thorns</i>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/866970716?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener"> A heartless 2.5 stars</a><br>2.<i>King of Thorns</i>- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/997982804" rel="nofollow noopener"> A dreadful 1 star</a><br>3. <i>The Emperor of Thorns</i> - <b>A Hateful 1 star</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512232281i/24585536._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://bookdragonsnest.squarespace.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/BookdragonSean" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/bookdragonsnest/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sean_thebookdragon/" rel="nofollow noopener">Insta</a> | <a href="https://york.academia.edu/SeanBarrs" rel="nofollow noopener">Academia</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16464390110036931653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1279246004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1279246004" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1279246004?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1279246004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3771061524286973187">This was a fantastic conclusion to what has turned out to be a very good series. It was a fantastically entertaining ride and Mark Lawrence succeeded in wrapping up all the ongoing story arcs in style. <br/><br/>Every four years members of The 100 meet in the holy city of Vyene, the heart of the Broken Empire, to vote. For over a century that vote has ended without anyone having the majority needed to claim the title of emperor. This time Honorous Jorg Ancrath is determined to see a different outcome. Jor</span>
  <span id="freeText3771061524286973187" style="display:none">This was a fantastic conclusion to what has turned out to be a very good series. It was a fantastically entertaining ride and Mark Lawrence succeeded in wrapping up all the ongoing story arcs in style. <br /><br />Every four years members of The 100 meet in the holy city of Vyene, the heart of the Broken Empire, to vote. For over a century that vote has ended without anyone having the majority needed to claim the title of emperor. This time Honorous Jorg Ancrath is determined to see a different outcome. Jorg travels with the votes of seven nations and is determined that no one will leave if he is not crowned emperor by votes end! He is not the only player in the game with an interest in the outcome. The mages continue their machinations from the shadows, the ghosts of the builders await the outcome for reasons of their own, and last, but definitely not least, the Dead King is heading to Vyene with his own plans to become emperor and he brings an army of the dead in his wake. <br /><br />It all combined to make an incredibly exciting story. This was again told in the first person from Jorg's POV. A ploy I have really enjoyed as it allows us to see a deeper side to Jorg and gives us the full chance to enjoy his unique wit and charm. I loved Jorg's development as a character. He is no hero, but he does finally show signs of growing into the role of anti-hero. More flashbacks provide more insight into Jorg's past and help us understand why he turned out as he did. <br /><br />Another real plus for this series has been the post-apocalyptic setting. At first it seems like a typical medieval fantasy world, but remnants of an advanced civilization remain for those that know where to look. I loved learning the final secrets this world had to offer. I also really enjoyed the balance of magic and old Builder technology. <br /><br />The ending was fantastic. A few of the final twists were a bit predictable, but despite that they were executed very well and I ended up really loving them. <br /><br />I was delighted to discover that Mark Lawrence has wrote a companion series set in this same fantastic world. I'll definitely be reading it!<br /><br />Rating: 5 stars. I feel at least one book in this series deserves a full 5 star rating! <br /><br />Audio Note: James Clamp has performed to a consistent level throughout the Broken Empire trilogy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3771061524286973187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1130750714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130750714" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1130750714?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781464033223" href="/book/show/18349868-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130750714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2019939334064694995">This novel helped me reach a new milestone in my life, and that is to enjoy listening to audiobooks. I've written several reviews of how much I hated audiobooks, but I believe James Clamp helped me realize how amazing audiobooks are. Add in the fact that this is an amazing novel with a terrific plot and characters. Kudos to Mark Lawrence for ending a trilogy the right way.<br/><br/>My journey with this trilogy was rough. I enjoyed the first novel very much, but the second left a bitter taste in my mouth. </span>
  <span id="freeText2019939334064694995" style="display:none">This novel helped me reach a new milestone in my life, and that is to enjoy listening to audiobooks. I've written several reviews of how much I hated audiobooks, but I believe James Clamp helped me realize how amazing audiobooks are. Add in the fact that this is an amazing novel with a terrific plot and characters. Kudos to Mark Lawrence for ending a trilogy the right way.<br /><br />My journey with this trilogy was rough. I enjoyed the first novel very much, but the second left a bitter taste in my mouth. It took me almost 2 years to pick this one and finally read the ending of the trilogy. I can gladly say though that the bitter taste is gone. <br /><br />I know it was a risk that I chose to listen to this rather than read it, but with my hectic schedule I didn't see a way for me to sneak this in my ever growing TBR pile. <br /><br />What makes this trilogy really amazing for me is Jorg. Jorg alone can make this trilogy standout among the others. He is gritty, profane, violent, and can be considered the devil himself. Without him, this trilogy wouldn't be as successful as it is today.<br /><br />There are other notable characters in this novel. I'm going on a whim and say that The Dead King really amazed me as a villain. Either it's James Clamp's narration that made him really interesting, or Lawrence has talent. I liked the twist and turns that he added. I didn't see the ending coming, even some of the minor plot twists. <br /><br />The writing is commendable. As good or even better than most of the notable fantasy authors out there. Consider the fact that this trilogy is considered as his debut trilogy, it's amazing how he managed to create such a masterpiece. I know I hated the second book, but after reading this, I might have to read it again and possibly change my opinion. <br /><br />The reason why this didn't get a 5 star from me is the same problem I had with King of Thorns, and that is the ever changing timelines. I hated it then, I still hate it now. It's more confusing when listening, but it was still confusing when I read it before, so it's not the audiobook that made it confusing. <br /><br />I don't want to talk about the ending anymore because I don't want to be the guy who spoils people. All I can say is that it's unexpected and gives closure to the trilogy.<br /><br />4/5 stars. A solid ending to a great trilogy. Highly recommended to fans of Joe Abercrombie and George RR Martin. If it's violence you're looking for, then this trilogy is for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2019939334064694995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3239375707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3239375707" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3239375707?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2020-shelf">2020-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3239375707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9923934436189304166">While this book might appear to be one of those love/hate things, I have to admit that Jorg, the character I love to hate, is awfully compelling.<br/><br/>Sure, he's a right bastard and he'll never mince words when the sword of the blade will do the job quicker, but beyond that, he's all about RESULTS. He never takes half-measures. Whether it's about living life, saving people, or murdering ANYONE who gets in his way, be they loyal or antagonistic, he never, ever, takes half-measures.<br/><br/>I admit I love that a</span>
  <span id="freeText9923934436189304166" style="display:none">While this book might appear to be one of those love/hate things, I have to admit that Jorg, the character I love to hate, is awfully compelling.<br /><br />Sure, he's a right bastard and he'll never mince words when the sword of the blade will do the job quicker, but beyond that, he's all about RESULTS. He never takes half-measures. Whether it's about living life, saving people, or murdering ANYONE who gets in his way, be they loyal or antagonistic, he never, ever, takes half-measures.<br /><br />I admit I love that about him. Sure, it means he'll kill everyone and anyone to get what he wants, but he NEVER goes back on his word. Of course, that is only a promise he makes to himself, and he has enough pride and bloodlust to put satan to shame, but it makes for a very compelling story.<br /><br />And then there's all the pure awesome going on with the worldbuilding: a broken future world after the bombs drop and something interestingly quantum opens up the door to belief and expectation altering reality, an amassed army of the undead ravaging this future medieval world, and even high-tech simulacra of men's minds trapped in machines.<br /><br />It's a heady mix and it's totally grimdark, but more than that, it's deliciously fun.<br /><br />Let's hear it for Jorg! He's a horrible man but damn, at least he never does anything by half-measures. <br /><br />Apparently, neither does Mark Lawrence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9923934436189304166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
