<div id="review_1775613755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1775613755" />
    <a title="Milda Page Runner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18708315-milda-page-runner"><img alt="Milda Page Runner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369856729p2/18708315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1775613755?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milda Page Runner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milda Page Runner" href="/user/show/18708315-milda-page-runner">Milda Page Runner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007503988" href="/book/show/21072991-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18708315-milda-page-runner?shelf=dark-and-gritty">dark-and-gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18708315-milda-page-runner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1775613755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3841763468041832527"><i>If you must run, have something to run toward, so it feels less like cowardice. And if you must run to something, why not make it the empire throne? Something suitably distant and unobtainable. After all, getting everything you wish for is nearly as dire a curse as having all your dreams come true.</i><br/><br/>Good and thought provoking book and a fitting ending to trilogy, although it didn’t blow my mind the way King of Thorns did. Whilst I enjoyed the story for the most part (except the gruesome bits) I fo</span>
  <span id="freeText3841763468041832527" style="display:none"><i>If you must run, have something to run toward, so it feels less like cowardice. And if you must run to something, why not make it the empire throne? Something suitably distant and unobtainable. After all, getting everything you wish for is nearly as dire a curse as having all your dreams come true.</i><br /><br />Good and thought provoking book and a fitting ending to trilogy, although it didn’t blow my mind the way King of Thorns did. Whilst I enjoyed the story for the most part (except the gruesome bits) I found conclusion somewhat unsatisfactory. Given how daring this story and the main character is – I was hoping for a really original, unpredictable, even shocking resolution and it didn’t quite live up to my expectations.<br />It is still a very good book and a must read to everyone who enjoyed (or managed to get through ;) Prince of Thorns.<br />Recommended for grim-dark fans.<br /><br /><i> ‘When you move the big pieces on the board, the world seems more like a game than ever. That illusion, that those at the top know what they’re doing – the feeling some folk hold, that the world is safe and solid and well-ordered – well, that illusion wears thin when it’s us who stand at the top doing the ordering. I don’t doubt that for every step you take toward Roma God sounds three steps further away.’ <br /><br />Words are blunt instruments, better suited to murder than to making sense of the world. <br /><br />We all carry the seeds of our own destruction with us, we all drag our history behind us like rusted chain. <br /><br />A man can reach into anything and turn it to his cause. It’s not want, or desire, just certainty. Only be assured that whatever you reach into will reach into you in turn. <br /><br />Anything that happens without witnesses never really happened at all. <br /><br /> ‘The future is a dark place. We all die there.’ <br /><br />There’s a slope down toward evil, a gentle gradient that can be ignored at each step, unfelt. It’s not until you look back, see the distant heights where you once lived, that you understand your journey.<br /><br />‘Dark times call for dark choices. Choose me.’<br /><br />We’re fashioned by our sorrows – not by joy – they are the undercurrent, the refrain. Joy is fleeting. </i><br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_761337063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/761337063" />
    <a title="Alicia Wanstall-Burke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21472787-alicia-wanstall-burke"><img alt="Alicia Wanstall-Burke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580473766p2/21472787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/761337063?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia Wanstall-Burke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia Wanstall-Burke" href="/user/show/21472787-alicia-wanstall-burke">Alicia Wanstall-Burke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761337063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14444572745470668315">I've made several manic recommendations to friends to read the Broken Empire Trilogy and whenever they ask 'Why?' or 'What is it about?' I find myself hard up against a roadblock.<br/>By roadblock I mean "giant choking lump in my throat every time I think about this series"...<br/><br/>Weird, given it isn't some navel-gazing, chic-lit, sob story, wah-wah examination of the world focussing on how we could and should be better humans. In fact, it's gory, unapologetic and painful. Sometimes even sickening. But th</span>
  <span id="freeText14444572745470668315" style="display:none">I've made several manic recommendations to friends to read the Broken Empire Trilogy and whenever they ask 'Why?' or 'What is it about?' I find myself hard up against a roadblock.<br />By roadblock I mean "giant choking lump in my throat every time I think about this series"...<br /><br />Weird, given it isn't some navel-gazing, chic-lit, sob story, wah-wah examination of the world focussing on how we could and should be better humans. In fact, it's gory, unapologetic and painful. Sometimes even sickening. But the Broken Empire is written with such grace that each page yields a quote of goose-bump inducing wisdom or humour or wit it almost seems impossible that one man could have created such characters. <br /><br />I haven't been so effected by a series since Rowen Cory Daniells' 'The T'en Trilogy', which I read as a teen. I was inspired then as I am inspired now. In my most humble opinion this series, the culmination of which is Emperor of Thorns, is a ground breaking work in Epic Fantasy. <br />I like it. I liked it so much I bought all the ebooks, then the hard covers. I liked it so fanatically, I ordered a signed/numbered copy from the UK. I've never done such a thing with a novel of any sort, and that alone should assure you it is worth the read. <br /><br />If my insistence is not sufficient, allow Jorg the time and he will change your mind. He is a character without equal. A boy, then man, so torn and damaged he is perfect. He will take you to places you weren't sure you could go, and then further again. He doesn't care what you think or feel along the way. If you desire a hero who is gentle, or polite, or kind, then perhaps you aren't meant for this narrative. <br />However if you remain on the ride, give him your heart and soul or even just a moment's trust, he will show what it is to be human. What it is to bleed and be real and how we can be better, one way or another.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14444572745470668315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1324857040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1324857040" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1324857040?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17267695-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1324857040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9162823087541125379">Emperor of Thorns was a satisfying conclusion. As the title of the book suggests, the inimitable Honorous Jorg Ancrath, was paving the way to getting himself crowned emperor of the broken empire at the Congression at the Gilden Gates of Vyene where the Hundred gather every four years to vote. The reason why the empire stayed broken till today was simply because no one ever managed to swayed a majority vote. However, this is Jorg we’re talking about, and this young man really knows how to play hi</span>
  <span id="freeText9162823087541125379" style="display:none">Emperor of Thorns was a satisfying conclusion. As the title of the book suggests, the inimitable Honorous Jorg Ancrath, was paving the way to getting himself crowned emperor of the broken empire at the Congression at the Gilden Gates of Vyene where the Hundred gather every four years to vote. The reason why the empire stayed broken till today was simply because no one ever managed to swayed a majority vote. However, this is Jorg we’re talking about, and this young man really knows how to play his hand - usually with much aplomb and not to mention quite a few deaths. <br /><br />The structure of the narration was similar to that of King of Thorns – present day, flashbacks and a female POV to widen the perspective, and in this case, it’s the necromantic arc with Chella. The Dead King finally made his appearance, along with a revelation of who he was. This plotline was built up with so much tension that the culmination of which was oddly disappointing as it felt too rushed. <br /><br />The whole concept around dreams continued to confound me more often than not. Coupled with the post-apocalyptic setting and foul necromantic arts, I find that the world-building of this series did not wholly resonate with me. What made me really like this series was Jorg – yes, just him mainly. This is a man of extremes, never given to moderate measures. He can kill at a whim, and is yet fiercely protective of those he loved. More so in this instalment than the preceding ones, there were instances where one discerned a spark of humanity and fallibility in Jorg. The complexity of his character was just so compelling.<br /><br />If you’re looking for a different spin on fantasy where the main character reads almost like villain, and one whom you’d want to root for at that, I wholeheartedly recommend The Broken Empire Trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9162823087541125379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1964360844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1964360844" />
    <a title="Mikheil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61494293-mikheil"><img alt="Mikheil" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1964360844?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikheil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikheil" href="/user/show/61494293-mikheil">Mikheil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1964360844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14679982444297581724">The Broken Empire trilogy is an amazingly well written, witty, rich with action and magic dystopia. <br/>A multitude of well developed, twisted and unique characters is what, in part, makes this series so interesting.<br/>We start our journey among a bloody brotherhood of the road, dumbfounded by disturbingly crude and grim narration of their atrocities, committed with unsettling triviality. LET THE ADVENTURE BEGIN. <br/>(I've noticed a lot of readers complaining about the "unnecessary and extreme" violence of</span>
  <span id="freeText14679982444297581724" style="display:none">The Broken Empire trilogy is an amazingly well written, witty, rich with action and magic dystopia. <br />A multitude of well developed, twisted and unique characters is what, in part, makes this series so interesting.<br />We start our journey among a bloody brotherhood of the road, dumbfounded by disturbingly crude and grim narration of their atrocities, committed with unsettling triviality. LET THE ADVENTURE BEGIN. <br />(I've noticed a lot of readers complaining about the "unnecessary and extreme" violence of the first chapter, but in the broken empire everything has a distinct purpose, even the cruelty). <br />The brothers and, brotherhood in general, are a leitmotiv of the trilogy, but what makes it truly idiosyncratic is the brother.<br />Honours Jorge Ancrath: what an amazing protagonist, one of the best antiheros out there. A very complex, multilayered, multifaceted, cunning character we just love to hate. <br />Throughout the trilogy we witness the progressive development of this ruthless, reckless, manipulative, devious thief, killer, rapist, manipulated, lost, traumatized, broken and consumed by guilt kid. <br />And we start to understand, to care, to wish brother Jorge to succeed, to chase his demons, to redeem himself, to serve his ultimate purpose and to finally be happy.<br />We complete our journey once again in a bloodshed and ruin, but with a remarkable context shifting: despite the sadness, there is hope. <br />In retrospective, as heartbreaking as it is, the shocking outcome is, fundamentally, the only possible conclusion for the story. <br />The Broken Empire trilogy is a highly entertaining, "can't let go till I'm done" series, that I would recommend to a fellow fantasy lover without hesitation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14679982444297581724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11643846776397301601" style="display:none"><i>“Life can tear away what’s vital to a man, hook it from him, one scrap at a time, leaving him empty-handed and beggared by the years. Every man has his thorns, not of him, but in him, deep as bones.” </i><br />3 stars<br />I don’t know why but for some reason, I just couldn’t really get into this book, which is a shame because I really liked the 2 previous books in the trilogy. Even though more things were supposed to happen, it just seemed a bit bleh to me…<br /><br />I started reading it a couple months ago, but couldn’t get past the first couple pages, which I thought was because of my reading slump, but however, this time, even when I was out of my reading slump, I had a hard time reading it; but I finished just for the sake of finishing the series (otherwise, it would have bothered the hell out of me for it to stay there for longer since I’m trying to reduce my ‘on-hold’ bookshelf)..<br /><br />Except for the ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ where Jorg sacrificed himself in order to restore order or for his child to stay safe (I felt that moment so much:( )  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> , it wasn’t that amazing of a book and the worst out of the 3, which is why I only rated it 3 stars (instead of 4&amp;5 in the previous books), and that fact is kind of disappointing because the trilogy started out really well :/<br /><br /><i> Would I re-read this trilogy anytime soon? </i> Eh, maybe… If I did, it would be the first &amp; second book mostly…<br /><br /><i> Would I read other books by this author? </i> Maybe, depending on the theme…</span>

<div id="review_391486686" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/391486686" />
    <a title="Milo " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6106947-milo"><img alt="Milo " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587052645p2/6106947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/391486686?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milo " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milo " href="/user/show/6106947-milo">Milo </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007439065" href="/book/show/15804760-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6106947-milo?shelf=notable-2013-releases">notable-2013-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6106947-milo?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6106947-milo?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6106947-milo?shelf=25-best-2013-releases">25-best-2013-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6106947-milo?shelf=2013-releases-read">2013-releases-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer391486686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14823422596632093866">The Review: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://thefoundingfields.com/2013/07/the-broken-empire-trilogy-emperor-of-thorns-by-mark-lawrence-advance-review-bane-of-kings/'>http://thefoundingfields.com/2013/07/...</a>. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“A stunning conclusion to the Broken Empire Trilogy. Easily one of the best books of 2013 – and a book that’s well worth the wait.”</i>
</b> ~The Founding Fields<br/><br/><br/>If I had to make a most anticipated list of Novels coming out this year, Emperor of Thorns would be in the Top 5, there’s no question about it. Mark Lawrence really impressed me with the first two books in the trilogy, both of which I own in hardback – so that I knew that Emperor of Thorns</span>
  <span id="freeText14823422596632093866" style="display:none">The Review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://thefoundingfields.com/2013/07/the-broken-empire-trilogy-emperor-of-thorns-by-mark-lawrence-advance-review-bane-of-kings/">http://thefoundingfields.com/2013/07/...</a>. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“A stunning conclusion to the Broken Empire Trilogy. Easily one of the best books of 2013 – and a book that’s well worth the wait.”</i>
</b> ~The Founding Fields<br /><br /><br />If I had to make a most anticipated list of Novels coming out this year, Emperor of Thorns would be in the Top 5, there’s no question about it. Mark Lawrence really impressed me with the first two books in the trilogy, both of which I own in hardback – so that I knew that Emperor of Thorns was always going to be a release day-buy for me. This will explain why I was so happy when I was able to get an Advanced Review Copy, so I’d like to start this review with a massive thank you to the kind folks over at Harper Voyager, and the author himself, so we could work something out. And does the book live up to my expectations? Oh, hell yes. It’s easily one of the best novels of the year, and with a year of some excellent books and we’re just over halfway through, that’s certainly saying something.<br /><br />"<i>To reach the throne requires that a man journey. Even a path paved with good intentions can lead to hell, and my intentions were never good.<br /><br />The Hundred converge for Congression to politic upon the corpse of Empire, and while they talk the Dead King makes his move, and I make mine. The world is cracked, time has run through, leaving us clutching at the end days, the future so bright that those who see it are the first to burn. These are the days that have waited for us all our lives. These are my days. I will stand before the Hundred and they will listen. I will take the throne whoever seeks to thwart me, living or dead, and if I must be the last emperor then I will make of it such an ending.<br /><br />This is where the wise man turns away. This is where the holy kneel and call on God. These are the last miles, my brothers. Don’t look to me to save you. Don’t think I will not spend you. Run if you have the wit. Pray if you have the soul. Stand your ground if courage is yours. But don’t follow me.<br /><br />Follow me, and I will break your heart.</i>"<br /><br />This is it, then. The last adventures of Jorg. Whilst I’m somewhat sad that there won’t be any more Broken Empire novels, as noted by the author himself, prequels or otherwise, it’s probably best that it ends at Book 3 rather than becoming an over-bloated series that readers quickly start to lose interest in the longer it goes. However, there is also the danger of a fantasy trilogy ending ‘too soon’ if you get what I mean. But thankfully, Lawrence brings it all to the table with a satisfying conclusion (don’t worry, I won’t spoil it), that really brings an end to this epic tale that will most surely be among the best fantasy works that I’ll read. I loved this trilogy, and I think with each instalment, it just gets better and better.<br /><br />Emperor of ThornsJorg’s character growth is incredible. He’s a rather unique main character for a story, often coming across as more of a downright villain than an anti-hero, and indeed – written by almost any other author, he would be. But the character himself is still as awesome as ever, and if you’ve enjoyed the last two books – then that’s what you should come to expect. It’s a strong, epic conclusion to the trilogy that really pulls out all the punches, where nobody is safe – and as we’re now all used to the major game players involved, Lawrence can waste no time with setting up future events (of course, no time was wasted setting up future events in the previous books as well), and instead create a compelling story that will draw the reader in, and not let up with the breakneck pace that this book moves along at.<br /><br />The author’s characters are well created, complex and far from the standard one-dimensional ones that litter poor novels. You’re not going to forget any of them in a hurry, and neither are you to forget The Broken Empire Trilogy anytime soon. It’s immense. Unpredictable. Captivating. A fitting conclusion. However you want to put it, the last adventure of Jorg of Ancrath is his best outing yet. Over the course of the trilogy, Lawrence has made himself a name to watch in fantasy, up there with the likes of Peter V. Brett, Brandon Sanderson, Joe Abercrombie &amp; George RR Martin. I can’t wait to see what he throws at the reader next, but it’s one that I’ll certainly be on board for.<br /><br /><b>VERDICT</b>: 5/5<br /><br /><b>THE BROKEN EMPIRE TRILOGY</b>: Prince of Thorns, King of Thorns, Emperor of Thorns<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14823422596632093866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_457155177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457155177" />
    <a title="Reader-ramble" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9590328-reader-ramble"><img alt="Reader-ramble" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404808831p2/9590328.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/457155177?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reader-ramble" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reader-ramble" href="/user/show/9590328-reader-ramble">Reader-ramble</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007439065" href="/book/show/15804760-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9590328-reader-ramble?shelf=must-reads">must-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer457155177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13960507127248254911">I've never done this before. I've never gotten a book ahead of its publication date. You can't leak the ending. You can't spoil it. So, what do you say? What do I say? In my previous reviews of <a href='http://militaryhousewriter.blogspot.com/2013/02/book-review-prince-of-thorns.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Prince of Thorns</a> and <a href='http://militaryhousewriter.blogspot.com/2013/05/book-review-king-of-thorns.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>King of Thorns</a> I brought up scenes I liked and wrote about Lawrence's use of modern science to make these books more than a fantasy. I even wrote about the chronological structure, but I'm not going to do that now.<br/><br/>I'm going to tell a story instead.<br/><br/>When I was sent a DM over twitter ask</span>
  <span id="freeText13960507127248254911" style="display:none">I've never done this before. I've never gotten a book ahead of its publication date. You can't leak the ending. You can't spoil it. So, what do you say? What do I say? In my previous reviews of <a href="http://militaryhousewriter.blogspot.com/2013/02/book-review-prince-of-thorns.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Prince of Thorns</a> and <a href="http://militaryhousewriter.blogspot.com/2013/05/book-review-king-of-thorns.html" rel="nofollow noopener">King of Thorns</a> I brought up scenes I liked and wrote about Lawrence's use of modern science to make these books more than a fantasy. I even wrote about the chronological structure, but I'm not going to do that now.<br /><br />I'm going to tell a story instead.<br /><br />When I was sent a DM over twitter asking if I wanted a copy, I naturally said yes. Then I ordered book two because I needed to catch up. <i>King</i> showed up before I left on vacation and I finished it before I got back. There, squished between the screen and front door, was a white shipping bag of bubble wrap and plastic. I couldn't get it open fast enough, and the damn package was impossible when I tried to use my fingers. So I resorted to scissors.<br /><br />My face lit up when I held the pretty green proof copy of <i>Emperor</i> in my hands. Sure, the release cover is nice looking, but it's always the story that matters. I couldn't wait to crack it open, but I did. I wanted time to devour it. The next day I sat down with it after work and ate it up.<br /><br />But then a curious thing happened. Over the course of the next few days, I read less and less. Then, about half way through, I set it down. It sat unread for a few days on my dining table. I walked by it every day, but didn't pick it up. Why did I stop reading? I was loving it to death.<br /><br />The truth was that I didn't want to get to the end. This is a strange feeling for me. I'm the kind of person who finished awful books because I have to know what happens next. I understand that a good thing must end because all things should end before they wear out their welcome. I'm the kind of person that would like more <i>Firefly</i>, but I'm happy it died while good so that fans didn't have to see it decay, a former shadow of its glory. I knew this was it for Jorg's story. I follow Lawrence on Twitter. He's already working on a new series.<br /><br />You see, we - the audience - has seen Jorg grow up. We haven't just seen a single moment in his life punctuated with memories. We know his thoughts and fears. We've seen him go from brash teenager who is way too smart, to a mature young man who recognizes all the wrong he has committed. A young man who recognizes the importance of having those you love in your life and why you should save them. Lawrence has managed to squeeze the life of a person into three books while at the same time analyze the role technological advances play in our world. It comes down to Jorg, the boy who defies fate and thumbs his nose at "No," to fix the mistakes that people made a thousand years ago. A boy-turned-man that is just like them, all desire, to fix modern man's drive to play god.<br /><br />Now, for those of you who don't like these books because Jorg is a deplorable personality, you miss the point. You put it down at <i>Prince of Thorns</i> and missed one of the best things about this character. He is self aware. He grew up and knows he is a terrible human being. He doesn't try to justify it or spout excuses. He knows. That is one of the best things about this character. As much as he tries to be a better person, he knows that he is impulsive, quick to anger, and contrary. He knows that people deserve better than him, yet he is the perfect hero for a story like this. And he knows that too. He is greedy, lustful, stubborn, and profane. He is human. You aren't supposed to like him, just understand him.<br /><br />So, in my own self awareness, I finished the book. The ending snuck up much faster than I imagined. At one moment I had one hundred pages, and then forty. And then there were no more. That left me staring at the back of a flimsy paper cover. I didn't want that to be it. Even with a favorite TV show, I don't think I've never been this attached. I cherish what I got and leave it at that. After all, all good things must end.<br /><br />But there was something stunningly beautiful about the ending. I wouldn't change a thing. And for that, I respect you Mark Lawrence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13960507127248254911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1140837171?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liviu Szoke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liviu Szoke" href="/user/show/16959770-liviu-szoke">Liviu Szoke</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18978552-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16959770-liviu-szoke?shelf=fantasy-reads">fantasy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16959770-liviu-szoke?shelf=fantasy-masterworks">fantasy-masterworks</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1140837171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13553551595164014632">Brilliant though unexpected ending for one of the most beautiful and violent fantasy series I have ever read. Everything fits perfect, from de characters' destinies to the plot's ending. And the SF elements are also perfectly integrated, making this story even more intriguing. Despite Jorg Ancrath being despised by a lot of people, I think he is the most interesting character ever to step between the pages of a book. Highly recommended.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_592110045" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/592110045" />
    <a title="Bob/Sally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally"><img alt="Bob/Sally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598307870p2/2224905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/592110045?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob/Sally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob/Sally" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally">Bob/Sally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2224905-bob-sally?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2224905-bob-sally?shelf=fantasy-grimdark">fantasy-grimdark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer592110045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5526711432981890023"><i>‘Dark times call for dark choices. Choose me.’</i><br/><br/>For all you Jorg haters out there, that one line, that simple declaration, sums up The Broken Empire better than anything I might be able to coax from my tired brain. Yes, for the second night in a row, a book has gotten its hooks into me and demanded I stay up far too late reading the final 200 pages. Fortunately, Emperor of Thorns delivered in almost every respect, defiantly answering my every conflicting emotion resulting from its predecessor, Kin</span>
  <span id="freeText5526711432981890023" style="display:none"><i>‘Dark times call for dark choices. Choose me.’</i><br /><br />For all you Jorg haters out there, that one line, that simple declaration, sums up The Broken Empire better than anything I might be able to coax from my tired brain. Yes, for the second night in a row, a book has gotten its hooks into me and demanded I stay up far too late reading the final 200 pages. Fortunately, Emperor of Thorns delivered in almost every respect, defiantly answering my every conflicting emotion resulting from its predecessor, King of Thorns.<br /><br />Mark Lawrence has taken the successful formula of the first two books, tweaked it, twisted it, and triumphed over the most problematic - and predictable - portions. Once again we find ourselves on a journey, but it's rediscovered some of the novelty and macabre sense of wonder that made the first book so fun. As was the case with the first two books, we have two interwoven stories, but whereas I found the flashback portion of the second book a bit weak, here it's strong enough to carry a tale all on its own. As for my concerns about the artifacts of Builder technology playing such a crucial role in the climax of the first two books, I am very pleased to say that they've proven to be completely unfounded. In fact, what Lawrence does to bring that aspect of the tale to the forefront here is one of the novel's most pleasant surprises.<br /><br />Another pleasant surprise is the continuing growth of Jorg. Yes, he's a right royal bastard, and about as far from a knight in shining armor as you can get, but he's human. We saw some growth in the second book as he matured and grew into his role as king, but here we see him grow into the role of expectant father as well. Of course, that brings about a whole slew of issues, given his dark relationship with his own father, but Lawrence develops it well, making it a key focus of the story, without overdoing it. In fact, there are some very nice parallels with the first book, including a surprise appearance of the very carriage that carried Jorg's mother and brother to their doom. Sadly, Miana feels a bit wasted here, given her developed in the last book, but I thought Katherine's role in things was very nicely played out, with more than a few surprises.<br /><br />An even darker book than the first two, with the Dead King's armies sweeping across the land, Emperor of Thorns still manages to provide a little dark humor, and even some genuine emotion along the way. I could have done without the interludes of Chella's story, but that's a minor quibble on my part. As for the climax . . . well, there are really two endings to the tale, both of which are extraordinarily well played. Without getting into spoiler territory, the first is largely inevitable, but still a hell of a lot of fun to watch come to fruition, while the second is a complete and utter surprise, an entirely bold choice on Lawrence's part to provide a note of finality to things.<br /><br />I said in my review of King of Thorns that it was a bigger book than the Prince of Thorns in every respect, and a tale that leaves even bigger expectations. Well, even if this is a somewhat smaller and more intimate tale, it more than manages to deliver on those expectations. An entirely satisfying conclusion to an original and exciting saga. Highly recommended.<br /><br /><br /><i>Originally reviewed at <a href="http://beauty-in-ruins.blogspot.ca/2013/08/jorg-finds-fitting-end-in-emperor-of.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Beauty in Ruins</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5526711432981890023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1893652238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1893652238" />
    <a title="Amit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56004712-amit"><img alt="Amit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463918672p2/56004712.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1893652238?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amit" href="/user/show/56004712-amit">Amit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1893652238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16813409639272912529">I unfortunatley lack the time to elaborate, so I'll make this short.<br/>Thank you Mark Lawrence, for one <b> GLORIOUS </b> trilogy. I'm absolutely confident that had the books weren't dark enough to diminish their audience, they were as popular as other awesome "mainstream" series (Sanderson's, Rothfuss's, Lynch's, etc.) <br/><br/>The biggest non-spoiler question in these books is: how <i> in hell </i> do we get to root (and dare I say, love) for Jorg's success? That awful murderer, rapist, monster. <br/><br/><i> “It's what I am, and i</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16813409639272912529" style="display:none">I unfortunatley lack the time to elaborate, so I'll make this short.<br />Thank you Mark Lawrence, for one <b> GLORIOUS </b> trilogy. I'm absolutely confident that had the books weren't dark enough to diminish their audience, they were as popular as other awesome "mainstream" series (Sanderson's, Rothfuss's, Lynch's, etc.) <br /><br />The biggest non-spoiler question in these books is: how <i> in hell </i> do we get to root (and dare I say, love) for Jorg's success? That awful murderer, rapist, monster. <br /><br /><i> “It's what I am, and if you want excuses, come and take them.” </i><br /><br />The answer hides in the perspective. Had Jorg been a real person in our world, we'd definitely loathe him. As a main character in a book, on the other hand, we <i> become </i> Jorg. And the more we experiece the world from his eyes, the more the answer gets clearer.<br /><br />The end of the third book, and of the trilogy as a whole, shattered me. I won't reveal anything, only assure you its a once-in-a-lifetime ride. I can't thank the author enough for what he created, and I'm so glad to know he wrote another trilogy in that world (whice I'll read ASAP!)<br />That's all, folks.<br /><br /><i> “Every man has his thorns, not of him, but in him, deep as bones.” </i><br /><br />No regrets.<br />Ruthless. Fearless. <br />Glorious.<br />Five stars and beyond.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16813409639272912529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2941409810" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2941409810" />
    <a title="Conor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30552336-conor"><img alt="Conor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400278909p2/30552336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2941409810?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor" href="/user/show/30552336-conor">Conor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2941409810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6193770792571979975">Great ending to one of the best fantasy series I've read. One of the few occasions in fantasy when a trilogy didn't somehow turn into 19 books, 3 novellas and a papyrus scroll. That (relative) brevity allowed this series to go out on a high and without any major drag in the middle. <br/><br/>As with the previous books in the series this one was driven by the protagonist Jorg. I wouldn't call him my "favourite" fantasy protagonist in terms of wanting to be mates with him but he was undoubtedly one of the m</span>
  <span id="freeText6193770792571979975" style="display:none">Great ending to one of the best fantasy series I've read. One of the few occasions in fantasy when a trilogy didn't somehow turn into 19 books, 3 novellas and a papyrus scroll. That (relative) brevity allowed this series to go out on a high and without any major drag in the middle. <br /><br />As with the previous books in the series this one was driven by the protagonist Jorg. I wouldn't call him my "favourite" fantasy protagonist in terms of wanting to be mates with him but he was undoubtedly one of the most complex and compelling protagonists I've read. This book saw more layers of complexity added to Jorg's ruthless, black-hearted character which was established in the first book. Time, the deaths of so many of his friends and the birth of his son haven't so much mellowed Jorg as given him new perspectives on life and he spends much of this book caught between a desire to make up for the crimes of his past and ..... a desire to do more horrible shit to fulfill his ambition and thirst for revenge.<br /><br />Full review to come ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="6193770792571979975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2521209702" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2521209702" />
    <a title="Antigone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22009196-antigone"><img alt="Antigone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383249021p2/22009196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2521209702?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Antigone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Antigone" href="/user/show/22009196-antigone">Antigone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425256541" href="/book/show/18342280-emperor-of-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22009196-antigone?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2521209702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3796124718943913705"><i>Time heals all wounds, but often it's only by the application of the grave, and while we live some hurts live with us, burning, making us twist and turn to escape them. And as we twist, we turn into other men.</i><br/><br/>The final volume of Mark Lawrence's <i>The Broken Empire</i> trilogy nudges Jorg Ancrath even further down the brutal road of his life. Twenty now, and king of seven nations, his lust for power drives him to pursue the most coveted crown in the land. There has been no emperor in recent memory. Tho</span>
  <span id="freeText3796124718943913705" style="display:none"><i>Time heals all wounds, but often it's only by the application of the grave, and while we live some hurts live with us, burning, making us twist and turn to escape them. And as we twist, we turn into other men.</i><br /><br />The final volume of Mark Lawrence's <i>The Broken Empire</i> trilogy nudges Jorg Ancrath even further down the brutal road of his life. Twenty now, and king of seven nations, his lust for power drives him to pursue the most coveted crown in the land. There has been no emperor in recent memory. Though the leaders of every nation congregate regularly to vote a man in, no candidate has received the quorum required to ascend the throne. It's the only challenge left in the world that proves seductive enough to lift the crafty Jorg to his feet and set him into motion.<br /><br />Lawrence remains faithful to his vision straight through to the end. His is a violent, post-apocalyptic civilization filled with malicious figures whose primary goal is to claw their way to a better weapon with a sharper edge. Plenty are the scenes of torture and abuse; not a single soul is spared its share of atrocity or the scars such sins produce. That Jorg Ancrath might choose to reign over such a nightmare speaks directly to his own damage and his inability to see beyond the demonic forces that consume him. He exists, in large part, merely as a funnel for pain - what flows into him from one source soon flows out again to be delivered upon another. And that's been interesting to watch because it strains the boundary surrounding the conventional anti-hero. Lawrence hazes the line between rebel and predator, relentlessly testing the moral flexibility of his reader, and resisting all enticement to put the question to bed.<br /><br />The problem, however, with ensnaring your readership in an ongoing ethical conundrum is that it prevents them from making a connection. You can prick at convention all you like, if you don't give your audience something to invest in they're simply not going to invest - and it's not going to matter how you end the thing or what happens to these questionable characters. It's just going to sort of be <i>over</i>. And some of us are just going to sort of be <i>relieved</i>, you know? Because that's how you feel when you're finally off the hook.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3796124718943913705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UEexIAUEE1ZPQaA9FvJM1tkRN566LLPBFDYo/mb3I7SCfK8B5OSIO9TTeu+BZkRpcm0LkKQ6JG06wMiIsro9yQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xBJi7i6X11KgSp4WS31gGBXQP6w5YDYAKI/lB00KtAIWKXzPz3dMPzvYRMTc6WinvqwDoid2oawGeQVxmUeqfw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Now he is eighteen—and he must hold on by strength of arms to what he took by torture and treachery.\n\nKing Jorg is a man haunted: by the ghost of a young boy, by a mysterious copper box, by his desire for the woman who rides with his enemy. Plagued by nightmares of the atrocities he committed, and of the atrocities committed against him when he was a child, he is filled with rage. And even as his need for revenge continues to consume him, twenty thousand men march toward the gates of his castle. His enemy is far stronger than him. Jorg knows that he cannot win a fair fight.\n\nBut he has found, in a chamber hidden beneath the castle, ancient and long-lost artifacts. Some might call them magic. Jorg is not certain—all he knows is that the secrets they hold can be put to terrible use in the coming battle…<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"8039570669532301729\" href=\"#\"   <!--
This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
